Business News

Finance: Rumors of Central Bank Opening for Cash Cause Gold Price to Fall First, Then Rise 192

—Result: Rebound of 1.1 Yuan—

The gold market still fluctuated yesterday. Reports indicated that the news was not optimistic, and people's hearts were not boosted. The price once broke through the 80 yuan mark. Large players took advantage of the low price to maintain the market. Rumors of the Central Bank opening for cash were constantly spreading. As a result, the price rebounded. Initially, the overseas silver market was flat in both England and the United States. Large speculators said that there were still buyers after the market closed at the listed price, but sellers demanded an additional 0.0625. The forward silver price in London rose by 0.5 to 1.5 cents. Exchange rates declined uniformly. The price of raw gold in London rose by half a penny. People's hearts were still tired. Over-the-counter trading opened at 83.4 yuan. Huixiang, Chunyuan, Yongfuxing, Yongheng, and others sold and retreated to within 3 yuan. Dada and Fuyu still bought, which helped to support the market. The market was still flat after the opening. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced, with both England and the United States rising, and the customs gold unit falling by 1.3 cents. The standard gold price street listing price was lowered to 914.5 yuan. It was even more difficult to boost people's hearts. Retail investors sold first, and the market became loose. Large players also competed to sell slightly. Sassoon and others sold off, and the exchange rate was chaotic, gradually retreating into the 80 yuan mark. Buyers maintained the market when they saw the low price, and banks also bought. The price was soon pulled up. It was known in advance that the HSBC's listed prices rose by 0.125 for England and 0.1875 for the United States. Sellers were still eager, and the daily market also sold off, but the market was still tired. Large players still had strong buying intentions. The price rebounded once after that, but the daily market took advantage of the high price to sell off, and the exchange rate was difficult to tighten. The supply gathered, and the price gradually went downstream, but it did not break the 80 yuan mark. There was still support after the low price. The domestic market was flat and gradually improved. The Indian silver market was predicted to remain unchanged and switched markets. However, the market was still weak at the noon close. Initially, the after-market was still flat due to large players selling off. Later, due to rumors that the Central Bank was opening for cash and that a certain bank was buying bullion, people's hearts were boosted and buying sentiment was stimulated. Although the Indian silver market reported no change, the price rose sharply. Banks took advantage of the high price to sell off US exchange, and sellers took advantage of the high price to sell off, gradually weakening. Finally, although Qiao Zhichifu sold off shillings, the market remained stable and fluctuated due to the strong buying interest of banks. The Indian silver market reported a rise of one anna for the second time, which had little impact. The market conditions for the day are recorded below:

The morning opening was 883.3 yuan, down 0.3 yuan from the previous close. Although Fuyu bought up to 3.5 yuan, the Central Bank's listed prices fell by 1.3 cents. Retail investors sold immediately and the market became tired. Yuanmao, Yongdingkang, Dadecheng, Fuxing, Yongli, Dada, and others sold and fell further. Sassoon sold off October shillings at 6.875, lowering the price to 79.1 yuan. Yingxiang, Dadecheng, Yongli, Fuyu, Huixiang, Hengyu, Dada, Chunyuan, Yong, and others took advantage of the low price to buy, gradually rising to 83 yuan. It was known in advance that HSBC's listed prices rose by 0.125 for England and 0.1875 for the United States. Fuxing, Yongheng, and others sold bullion at high prices, lowering the price to 1.3 yuan. Spring and Autumn

A Talk with Princess Der Ling 201

— (Ji Ping)

The news that Princess Der Ling, the original author of our journal's long-form novel "The Fragrant Clouds of Imperial Incense," has come to Shanghai from America was announced a few days ago. I think all our readers will certainly have had their curiosity piqued about all things related to her, and can't wait to catch a glimpse of her charm. Having served Empress Dowager Cixi for over two years in the palace, she recorded the Empress Dowager's personality, hobbies, etc., in exhaustive detail. Those who love and continue to read "The Fragrant Clouds of Imperial Incense" will admire her writing ability, which is far beyond that of ordinary people. Indeed, as a woman of her caliber, she has written as many as seven or eight novels, and is still a special writer for newspapers in the United States, and she also has to return to China to search for materials for novels; that kind of spirit is worthy of admiration by writers!

Yesterday afternoon, I visited the Princess at the Cathay Hotel, wanting to offer this material to those interested. Because she was preparing to leave for Peiping, and her journey was rushed, the time to talk was very short, and what I wanted to talk about had to be left for next time. First, I must introduce what kind of person she is. In a nutshell, she is completely a Europeanized woman. Her speech, clothing, and manners are all like those of a Western woman. Of medium height, neither fat nor thin, about forty years old, but her face is still gorgeous, always exuding a gentle and pleasant expression, with not a trace of aristocratic air.

She said that she rarely read Chinese newspapers while staying in the United States, but after arriving in Shanghai and browsing the Shen Bao, she felt that the compilation and printing were good. In particular, the pictorial magazine was as exquisite as those in the United States, and could truly represent China's new printing industry. I told her that "The Fragrant Clouds of Imperial Incense" had been published for more than a year, and the reporter had a very good impression of it, and perhaps it would be printed as a single volume in the future. She was very happy about it. Then she said: Having left the country for eight years, seeing the scenery of Shanghai, it is very different. Coming here and talking with many old friends, she expressed her sympathy for the current situation of the motherland. She had also been to the new city center, which fully demonstrated the progress of Chinese construction. She had heard that the capital was showing new signs, and when she went north to Peiping and south, she would be able to freely travel to the scenic spots of the capital. In short, the amusement of these few days has already made a deep impression, proving that my repeated broadcasts in the United States, promoting China, are by no means all deceptive pretense.

Finally, she said that when she comes to Shanghai next time, she will make an appointment to talk in detail, which will surely satisfy the information for you to write. We shook hands and said goodbye.

Thirty Li by Sailboat 202

— Qiao Yuncan

Sailboats have become obsolete means of transport in our era; however, in remote towns and villages, and under special circumstances, there are still times when they are needed; that kind of elegance is something that even battleships and large freighters cannot imagine. Last time, I hurried back to my hometown from Shanghai. I was used to the thirty li of a wheelbarrow's taste, and that morning, with the light still dim, I was already sitting securely in the cart, listening to the sound of the axle pressing on the winding paths in the fields, with the rice paddies crisscrossing like embroidery, and the water-lifting devices answering with songs. A gentle breeze brushed my clothes, and I was beginning to enjoy the scene when, in an instant, dark clouds spread out, and before I knew it, a swift wind and heavy rain descended like a flying general, relentlessly attacking me! The cart puller and I really couldn't take it, so we hired a small "catch the fresh" sailboat, and I immediately abandoned the land and boarded the boat. Hilariously, it seemed that the heavens were deliberately making fun of me. Just as we raised the sail, the sun began to shine dimly again. There were three boatmen: one boss, one young apprentice, and one deckhand. The young apprentice steered, the boss rowed, and the deckhand went ashore to pull the rope, moving forward at a snail's pace. I was reminded of two sentences from a letter by Qiu Shuxuan, "Watching boats sail on the spring water is like sitting in heaven, and one does not know the hardships of the people on the boat!" Besides me, there was also a grocer on board. The boatman solemnly said, "The boat is small, and the river is wide, so it is easy to capsize. Gentlemen, please be calm and don't move around!" My weight was greater than that of the other passenger, so we moved a leather suitcase to balance things out. This is probably what is meant by "crossing the river in the same boat."

There were ditches and wooden signs on both sides of the bank. The boatman pulling the rope was very difficult, but he rowed the boat quickly, like an ape climbing, truly showing the skill of "a fist never leaving the hand, and a song never leaving the mouth!" Not until noon did we reach a market. We disembarked to catch our breath and ate two bowls of noodles to fill our stomachs. The small teahouse was still not open for the morning market. Next to it sat a table of tea drinkers from the town, one of whom, wearing a Zhongshan suit and sporting a small mustache, was there pontificating as if he were a modern reviewer. They did not linger. We returned to the boat, and the boatmen were also eating large pancakes to fill their stomachs, dipping their hands into the river to scoop up water to quench their thirst. That day, at dusk, we finally reached our destination.

Always these words! Annoying

An Explanation of the Plot of "Si Lang Visits His Mother" 203

— (Xin Yu)

The article "Errors in 'Si Lang Visits His Mother'" published in Spring and Autumn on the 27th, I fear, is due to a misunderstanding of the plot of the play. Now I will specially state its meaning below. When the Yang family and his sons were defeated, Si Lang was captured, changed his surname to Muyi, and was recruited by Xiao Bang as his son-in-law. He often missed his relatives, but could not return. When Xiao Tiansuo led his troops to fight against Xiao Bang, She Taijun escorted grain and came to the Northern Frontier. Therefore, in the lyrics of the play, there are singing lines such as: "Xiao Tiansuo, set up Tianmen, the two countries will fight, Old Lady, escorting paste, coming to the Northern Frontier." Si Lang heard that his mother had come to the north and wanted to see her very much, but he had no permit and could not pass the border. He then discussed it with the princess and designed to steal the permit, which then led to the various plots of passing the border, seeing his mother, and returning the permit.

Little Western Paradise 204

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: The Great Member Cherishes His Feathers, Skirmishing Skillfully; New Love is Separate from Flesh and Blood, Visiting the Sick Without a Way.

Duo Cai walked to his side and gently patted his shoulder, saying, "People say you are a child, but you really act like a child? If you don't cry or make trouble, wouldn't you be a very good person? That way, you can easily gain people's favor." Yueying thought of the sentence "the bones are all his." She didn't dare to say anything more, but only lowered her head and stood quietly by his side, her hand fiddling with her own clothing buttons. Duo Cai saw that he was as docile as a sheep, and regardless of being alone there, he stroked his hair again, and even sniffed at his temples with the tip of his nose. Shi Lian saw this, and knew that Duo Cai was already happy, so he immediately held the package of cosmetics on the table with both hands, and cupped his hands towards Yueying, saying, "I'm really not offering anything special, but congratulations to the two of you on your wedding." Duo Cai smiled, "You're being too polite. Didn't you send a gift two days ago?" Shi Lian laughed, "No, there should be a distinction. That was a gift for your wedding, and this is a gift for your honeymoon. To tell you the truth, in a few days, I will also send a gift for the new wife's pregnancy." Duo Cai said, "How would you know if he is pregnant?" Shi Lian blushed and said, "Did you think I said something wrong again? If the new wife is pregnant, it will always be revealed sooner or later, so wouldn't I know?" Yueying only let them joke around, but didn't say a word. Shi Lian still placed the cosmetics on the table, and then became serious, saying, "Duo Cai, we are always close friends. If you have any difficult things, as long as I can do it, I can do it for you. I'm going to go to the new wife's house to take a look now. If you have anything, just tell me, and I will do my best." 御香縹緲錄 (Fragrant Whispers from the Imperial Court) 205

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Is it really worthwhile to expend so much manpower on artistic pursuits? Besides this, what other uses do the eunuchs have? These two questions are not easy to answer. But in my opinion, the answer to the first question should be positive; because if so much manpower wasn't spent, how could more than three thousand pots of colorful and pleasing chrysanthemums bloom? Moreover, these chrysanthemums can at least bring some joy to the Empress Dowager, which makes it very worthwhile!

Chapter 34: Jade Body Stretched Out

When I first entered the palace as an attendant lady-in-waiting by the Empress Dowager's decree, I naturally felt constrained and awkward in everything I did. The most difficult thing was the matter of bathing. Because my sister and I had lived abroad for a long time, we had developed a habit of bathing every day. Unfortunately, I didn't ask my father about this beforehand, so after entering the palace, I deeply felt the inconvenience the next morning. My sister and I searched for a long time, but couldn't find a set of bathing utensils in the huge palace. Perhaps the palace maids and eunuchs each had these things, but they only used them privately, and didn't dare to bring their own for us to use. Helpless, we had to endure it for the time being. But I felt very puzzled. Could it be that the other ladies-in-waiting who came before us didn't bathe all year round? Or could it be that they all went home to bathe? Then what about Longyu and Consort Jin? (420)

婦人心 (A Woman's Heart) 206

— Allegory

There was a Mrs. Li living in the east neighborhood. She had an eighteen-year-old daughter who went out every day dressed coquettishly. But people rarely saw her when she came back, because she was a dancer. Doing this profession did bring in a lot of income, at least two or three hundred yuan a month. Mrs. Li would always smile gleefully when she talked about her daughter.

There was a Mrs. Wang living in the west neighborhood. She had a son. She painstakingly nurtured him until he graduated from middle school, but after graduation, he couldn't find a job for two years. Mrs. Wang ran around, asking relatives and friends to find a position for her son. Until now, he has finally found a job as an accounting assistant in a department store. Her son works diligently, going out early and returning late, but he only earns eighteen yuan a month. Mrs. Wang thought that Mrs. Li in the east neighborhood didn't teach her daughter much, and heard that she didn't even graduate from elementary school. Now she is a dancer, and her monthly income is more than ten times that of her middle school graduate son. She couldn't help but sigh with emotion, saying, "It's better to give birth to a daughter than a son." —

風土小誌 (Local Customs)

日本的迎神賽會 (Japanese Festival) 207

— Kichiun

Anyone who hasn't been to Japan wouldn't believe that the Japanese are more superstitious than we are. In addition to the household gods in every home, stone Jizo Bodhisattvas can be seen everywhere. In the countryside, on the banks of fields and next to outhouses, you can see several stone Buddhas that are three feet tall. The shrines are very large, with two or three in each district. They are like our ancestral halls, probably enshrining the emperors and past sages of Japan. University students in square hats, gentlemen in Western suits, also put their hands together and pay their respects and give alms there.

Each shrine has a specific festival day, lasting for three days before and after, as lively as our temple fairs. At night, the streets are full of vendors selling toys and goods. So when the festival arrives, it is a happy day for children. Each household hangs a round paper lantern outside the door, with a cluster of paper flowers on it, which are hung by people sent by the neighborhood association. Both items cost one yuan and two jiao. Roughly, one lantern is hung per house. Shops with larger frontages hang two or more lanterns.

On the festival day, the shrine's hall is brightly lit with candles. Two flagpoles are erected outside the door, with colored ribbons hanging from them. Outside the hall are five long banners, with dragons, phoenixes, turtles, and qilin embroidered on the red silk. The middle one is embroidered with five butterflies, probably representing "five bats bringing blessings." Pearl curtains hang low inside the hall, and the contents are unknown. Next to the hall is a stage, only shoulder-high, with three people playing drums and flutes. A woman is wearing a white gauze dress with a bright red underskirt. She has a copper hoop on her head, and her hair is tied into braids with white paper. Sometimes she holds a tin staff, sometimes a bow and a fan. She is performing on stage to the music, without uttering a sound, probably a drama to entertain the gods.

The neighborhood association is a community organization formed by the residents of the neighborhood, managing streetlights and sanitation, and the festival is also an important task. A high platform is set up at the entrance of the alley, with five people sitting on it, one playing a small gong, one playing a flute, and the rest mostly playing drums. It is the pure sound of Japanese entertainment for the gods. It looks like the Taiping ritual played in Shanghai's alleys. The music sounds like the drummers in a funeral home in our country, which is quite amusing. A reed mat shed is set up on the open ground to serve as the festival's office and hall. In the middle is enshrined a deity tablet written on white paper, and on the offering table are two bottles of wintergreen leaves, with foot-long white paper rolls inserted in copper vases, like a pair of white candles. Gifts sent by nearby shops and residents, foot-wide steamed buns and pink pastries, are all placed in high-legged wooden plates. Gifts include watermelons, pears, apples, squid, etc. Those who send cash have their names and amounts posted on the wall, which is the same as in our country. A large copper drum and a palanquin are also placed in the reed shed, which are important items for the festival.

Large copper drums are found in temples in our country, with frames, railings, and four casters underneath. The palanquin is like our incense pavilion, with a brass phoenix on top and copper bells hanging all over the corners. It is finely carved and lacquered with gold and black paint. There are many carrying poles, usually displayed in the shrine on wooden benches. The inside of the pavilion is empty, allowing it to sway freely when carried. These copper drums and palanquins are very expensive, costing over a thousand yuan, which is not surprising. Palanquins are divided into two sizes, the small ones are only three or four feet square, carried entirely by twelve or thirteen-year-old children, which is very interesting.

During the festival, the first person carries two pieces of wood, striking them to direct the procession forward. Several other people carry tin staffs like those of the Mulian monks, the purpose of which is unknown. Next comes the copper drum, pulled slowly by dozens of five or six-year-old children wearing beautiful clothes and white socks. Their heads are either covered with paper hats or tied with colored cloth. One person beats the drum, striking it three times on the drum and then three times on the side, repeating this cycle. Behind the copper drum is the palanquin, carried by twenty or thirty boys, each shouting "Ya! Ya!" The palanquin does not proceed in a straight line, and everyone can freely rush east and west, going from the upper street to the lower street, often rushing into people's gates or knocking down pedestrians. Especially when passing through the bustling streets, in addition to the horses and carriages stopping at any time, there are several policemen in white clothes who follow them all day long to supervise them. The girls pulling the copper drum are too young, and some are led by their mothers and sisters, and those who can't walk sit in the copper drum frame to rest.

Some people prepare several buckets of cold water at the door, waiting for the palanquin to come and pour it over everyone's heads. Then many "drenched chickens" carry the palanquin, rushing around and playing. Sometimes they shake the palanquin up and down, but fortunately the palanquin is sturdy and there is no danger of it being damaged.

Page 17

自由談 (Free Talk)

交誼史話 (Historical Tales of Friendship) 208

— Lingjing

I think when people are most troubled, it is best to read history. Because the phenomena you see now or the things you encounter yourself certainly have precedents in history. The so-called "there is nothing new under the sun" is at least 90% true. If you don't believe it, look:

Historical Records, Biography of Li Shang: "Shang's son, Ji, styled Kuang, was on good terms with Lü Lu. When Empress Dowager Gao died, the ministers wanted to kill the Lü clan. Lü Lu was a general, stationed in the Northern Army. Grand Commandant Zhou Bo was not allowed to enter the Northern Army, so he sent someone to kidnap Li Shang, ordering his son Kuang to deceive Lü Lu. Lü Lu believed him, so he went out with him. Then Grand Commandant Zhou Bo waited to enter and seize the Northern Army, and then killed the Lü clan. That year, Shang died and was given the posthumous title of Marquis Jing. His son Ji succeeded him as marquis. The world called Li Kuang a seller of friendship."

This is a historical fact from the Han Dynasty. Sima Qian seems to disapprove of Li Kuang's actions, angrily commenting that he sold his friendship. In fact, this was Zhou Bo's cunning plan. If Li Kuang had not been moved that day, his father would not necessarily have been killed by Zhou Bo. Perhaps Li Kuang did not see this at first. He only compared the relationship between father and son and the relationship between friends, and felt that it was always worth exchanging a friend's life for his father's life, so he resolutely followed Zhou Bo's plan. Ban Gu praised Li Kuang's actions as "loyalty to the ruler and parents," which is absolutely not to be blamed. However, Su Dongpo greatly disapproved of Ban Gu's defense. See Su Lao's Dongpo Zhilin:

"Ban Gu said, 'During the time of Emperor Xiaowen, the world considered Li Ji to be a seller of friendship. Selling friendship means seeing profit and forgetting righteousness. If Ji's father was a meritorious official and was also threatened, destroying Lü Lu to secure the state, loyalty to the ruler and parents is acceptable.' Dongpo said, 'At that time, Ji had to sell his friend. The fault lies in being the son of a meritorious official and associating with a national traitor, and being on good terms with him. Shi Que's son Hou associated with Zhou Yu. Que forbade him, but he did not listen and was eventually killed. The gentleman did not criticize him, saying that he extinguished relatives for righteousness. Li Shang's virtue is not as good as Shi Que, so Ji was spared from death. He was a lucky man of ancient times, and Gu is eager to wash away the stain of selling friendship. Gu's righteousness is shallow!'"

I think Ban Gu's defense is quite biased. Although the Lü clan was guilty and heinous as national traitors, Li Kuang certainly did not see this. Otherwise, he would not have associated with them. Therefore, Li Kuang's motive was based solely on a concept of family ties. The concept of the state did not exist. Ban Gu praised him as "loyalty to the ruler and parents," which naturally aroused Su Lao's usual indignation. Things like this are not uncommon in history, but there are some differences. For example, Li Zhu's selling of friendship was forced by circumstances. There was also Wang Dao's selling of Zhou Qi in the Jin Dynasty, which was entirely due to misunderstanding. Biography of Zhou Qi:

"When Wang Dun raised troops, Liu Wei advised the emperor to remove all the princes. Sikong Dao led his subordinates to the palace to plead guilty. He met Zhuan entering, and Dao called to Qi, saying, 'Boren, I entrust the lives of my entire family to you.' Zhuan went straight in without looking back. After seeing the emperor, he said that Dao was loyal and sincere, and pleaded for him greatly. The emperor accepted his words. Zhuan was happy, drank wine and went out drunk. Dao was still at the door and called to Qi again. Qi did not speak to him, but looked around and said, 'This year we will kill all the traitorous slaves and take gold seals as big as dippers to tie to our elbows.' After coming out, he submitted a memorial to the emperor, speaking very urgently about Dao. Dao did not know that he had saved him, and resented him greatly. After Dun achieved his ambition, he asked Dao, 'Zhou Qi has a reputation for being an outstanding talent in both the north and south. He should be promoted to the Three Dukes without any doubt.' Dao did not answer. He asked again, 'If he is not promoted to the Three Dukes, should he be made my subordinate?' He did not answer again. Dun said, 'If not, I will execute him!' Dao was silent again. Later, Dao checked the old records of the Secretariat and saw Qi's memorial, which pleaded for him earnestly and sincerely to the emperor. Dao held the memorial and wept, unable to control himself. He told his sons, 'Although I did not kill Boren, Boren died because of me. In the realm of the underworld, I owe this good friend!'"

This is a famous story. From Wang Dao's life and actions, we know that it was indeed due to a misunderstanding. Therefore, people still often use Wang Dao's two words of repentance as a self-redemption for unintentionally betraying a friend.

The two stories above, one due to force and the other due to misunderstanding, I think can still be given some degree of understanding. Only Yang Shan's selling of Zhang Pu in the Ming Dynasty makes me feel some "unforgivable" resentment.

Biography of Wang Yu: "Once, he studied under Fang Xiaoru. At that time, an imperial decree ordered the destruction of Fang Xiaoru's collection of writings, saying, 'Anyone who dares to collect it will be punished as a traitor!' The compiler Zhang Pu liked Xiaoru's writings and kept some at home. He spoke privately with his friend Yang Shan, and Shan borrowed them to read. He secretly reported it to the court. The emperor was angry and executed Pu in the market, while Shan was promoted to official. From then on, the world felt sorrow."

秋 (Autumn) 209

— Shen Shengshi

Again it is the season of lament,

Life is painted with weariness in the autumn wind;

Desolate life,

Thin poetic thoughts,

Hopeless days wither away with the fallen leaves.

Under the cool twilight starlight,

Crickets cry under the wall of the old house;

It is the same scene as the year before last,

A lonely heart,

Wanders in the twilight of insect sounds.

美底責任心 (三) (A Beautiful Sense of Responsibility (3)) 210

— Originally written by George Bernard Shaw, translated by Ting

——Did you even say one word in my defense?

——But don't you realize what will happen if you separate from her? You will lose the power to control her, and you will have to get a divorce.

——I don't have the power to control her now.

At this time, a clerk came in and said:

——A lady has come to see you, sir. He said emotionally, she is a very beautiful lady. Ah... sir. If she is in some trouble, please help her. If she is accused of something, please don't believe a word anyone says. I can guarantee her innocence with my own life.

The lawyer was almost speechless with surprise;

——Good... good! Really. Zhi Pi Jun! He calmed down slightly and said, what is her name?

——I forgot to ask her name, sir.

——Perhaps make an effort to remedy this oversight.

——I almost didn't dare to ask her, sir. It seemed like a kind of blasphemy. But I think—I hope—she will forgive me. Then he went outside.

The litigant said:

——She is my wife. She used to have feelings for that young madman. —The End—

鄉誼 (十) (Fellow Villagers (10)) 211

— Moying

I left Batavia in October, on the same hot days as usual. A rickety motorcar carried two desolate pieces of luggage, and sitting inside silently watching them were me and Genwu—one person seeing me off. Perhaps feeling that such silence was too terrible, Genwu took out his usual Elephant Brand cigarette, handed me one, borrowed a match from the Javanese driver, and lit it. A puff of gray smoke escaped from his mouth, disappearing in the dry weather. Then, as if it had reached a point where he had to say something, he pinched the half-smoked cigarette between his fingers and said in a low, weak voice that seemed tired from overwork:

"It's good for a person to go to a few more places. You're not young anymore, and there's no better opportunity for you to stay in Ji City... cough, but... you don't have enough experience, so you should be extra careful on the road. If you can meet a reliable person on the ship, like a fellow villager..."

"Yes, I think so too," I said. "Genwu, I'm a little scared. It's always a little... a little... to go to an unfamiliar place. The job you've already introduced me to: and it's also a Dutch territory, so it won't be troublesome to go ashore or anything, which makes me feel much more at ease."

"You can rest assured!" Genwu patted me on the shoulder.

We fell silent again. The car was really rickety, constantly shaking on the flat asphalt road to the port. Sweat trickled down my forehead, and the heat of the white light penetrated the car canopy, steaming our bodies. When the car arrived at the port—Tanjung Priok—I was almost completely soaked.

Not long before the ship was due to sail, after putting the luggage in the cabin, we sat down here.

"You have to keep an eye on the luggage, you know?" Genwu said.

"Yes. There are all kinds of people on the ship, so I should..." I replied to him, thinking in my heart, sitting in the steerage, the air is so bad, how can I bear it? What if I need to go up to the deck to get a breath of fresh air?

"But it would be good to find someone I know," Genwu continued.

I also hoped that a friend would unexpectedly appear here. I constantly looked around, paying special attention to anyone who walked past me. After half an hour, all we met were Javanese chattering in Javanese, Chaozhou people wearing padded jackets, and Bombay people wearing Turkish-style red-tasseled hats. The fact proved that our hopes could not be realized: I gritted my teeth, prepared to fully taste the bitterness of the trip, what else could I do?

The ship's whistle blew sharply, a burst of commotion, and most of the people seeing us off went down one after another.

"Genwu, goodbye."

"Goodbye! Write a letter immediately when you get there, you know?"

I nodded.

The sky had already darkened when we left Tanjung Priok port. Looking out from the small round window in the steerage, a deep blue sea was waving up and down. Although the wind at sea was strong, it couldn't reach us here. A smell of lacquer and the stench coming up from the cargo hold made people want to vomit. The electric light was yellow, illuminating the sallow faces and blue faces of the surrounding passengers. The women's hair was disheveled; some were simply like nightshades, with only the terrifying eyes that had lost their spirit and were sunk into their sockets. Then, without knowing which child started crying, crying so loudly that it made people feel extra annoyed. Sitting uncomfortably, I lay down on the hard iron plate, with an old mat resisting its coldness. I wanted to sleep, so I spent the night...

I really don't know when I fell asleep. When I woke up the next day, the ship had already left Batavia far behind. I took a face towel to the faucet to wash my face, thinking that there shouldn't be any danger to the luggage if I walked away for a while, so I dragged my shoes and walked up there.

Only a thin, long person with a buzz cut was brushing his teeth at the tap. The morning weather was very cool and the wind was strong, making me shiver when I walked in front of him. That person stopped what he was doing, looked up at me, and said with his mouth covered in white toothpaste foam:

"Is it very cold?"

Authentic native dialect!

This shocked me. I looked at this fellow villager, but he was very unfamiliar, as if I had never seen him before. I stood there, forgetting to wash my face.

"Not washing your face?"

After being reminded, I bent down, stretched out the face towel to the tap, wrung it out for a while, and wiped my face.

"You're also from XX, right?" I asked.

"That's right. I heard you speaking XX in the steerage yesterday. I wanted to greet you, but I was too embarrassed. Are you alone?" After saying that, he took a sip of water, gargled, and spat it into the sea.

"I'm alone. What about you?"

"Same as you." He was about to leave. But he said again: "Speaking of which, we're fellow villagers. So how can you not be lonely?"

"How can I not be lonely? It would be good if someone was together, not to mention anything else, it would be easier to pass the days by just talking."

"Then let's go down together."

水上夜曲 (Nocturne on the Water) 212

— Liang Qijun

An evening haze with the melancholic fragrance of lilacs slowly, gently, rose from the river. Gradually it spread further towards both banks.

Poplar trees, shrubs, reeds by the riverbank, a small bridge, an ancient city wall, all sketched out rough lines in a blurry pale gray. From these things, one could feel a kind of melancholy that sighed for the lateness of the hour.

Ya Heng's small boat had just slipped out of the bridge hole when Ya Ji hooked it with his long bamboo pole for punting the boat.

She shook her hand and said softly:

"Don't wake up Mom."

That one just smiled...

When the two boats were moving side by side, Ya Ji jumped over to the boat and embraced Ya Heng's full, mature body.

The boat moved violently, and Ya Ji's voice trembled as he spoke:

"You—are making—making me suffer so much."

Inside the cabin, there was the sound of turning over. He loosened his hands, and she took the opportunity to break free, slipped from the bow to the stern, and from the stern jumped onto his boat.

Spring flowers were blooming in Ya Ji's heart.

The intense color of the night deepened.

Only shadowy black shapes remained of the blurred outlines made of rough lines.

The moon hung high in the velvety soft sapphire-blue sky. The stars were smiling. The river caressed the edges of the boats, softly singing a serenade that could barely be heard.

The two sat side-by-side on the stern of the boat; four large thighs that had been sun-baked to a rose color made circles in the still water.

"Look." Ya Ji put one arm around Ya Heng's waist; one finger pointed at the horizon. "Tonight is the Qixi Festival. That bright, sparkling star is the Weaving Maid Star, and the one that is closely attached to it is—"

"The Cowherd Star?"

"Ah, yes, you're really smart. Little girl."

Ya Ji was pleased.

The blush on Ya Heng's face extended all the way to her ears.

After a long time, restless emotions could not withstand the erosion of silence.

Ya Ji spoke.

"Didn't your mother say that after I get rich, she would marry you to me?"

"No, my mother wants me to marry a rich man." Ya Heng said, pouting her small mouth. "You are as poor as we are..."

"But..."

Ya Ji took out two sparkling white silver dollars from his pocket.

"I like this." Ya Heng snatched them away.

"I like this—" Ya Ji's voice trembled again.

Suddenly, Ya Heng's long string of laughter was so seductive that the river was also moved. The small boat trembled, and the river gently soothed it.

A few small ferries were moored haphazardly at the foot of the city wall. An old woman poked her head out of the cabin.

"That boy from that family, what a shameless thing."

The river softly sang, the stars smiled, the moon shone.

It was autumn.

A cool autumn wind was blowing, but the autumn wind was still young.

申報本埠增刊 (Shen Bao Local Supplement)

談言 (Chatter)

A Plea for Renji Hospital 213

— Meng Ruo

Reports state that Shanghai Renji Hospital, after 91 years of dedicated service, is facing exceptional financial difficulties due to the current economic downturn. It is said that last year, the hospital, recognizing the difficulty in maintaining operations, made every effort to reduce all expenditures. However, on one hand, resources are scarce and income has decreased. On the other hand, demand exceeds supply, and expenses have actually increased. As a result, there is a shortfall of over 20,000 yuan, causing the authorities to feel the pain of having insufficient resources. This is a matter that deserves great concern.

Shanghai has several hospitals founded by foreigners, such as Renji, Guangren, Guangci, and the Women and Children's Hospital. They are established with benevolent intentions and offer very low fees to those seeking treatment, and in some cases, even provide free medical care and medicine. Their benefits to the common people are immense. Everyone knows that poor people living in Shanghai cannot afford to get sick. They certainly cannot afford doctors who charge two or three yuan for a consultation, nor can they afford medicine that costs one or two yuan per dose. Therefore, the general poor and working classes rely on these charitable hospitals for their health security.

Shanghai has many famous doctors and national experts, and at least several large-scale, well-equipped hospitals. However, most of them are aristocratic doctors or hospitals, catering only to a small number of wealthy individuals. The cost of their medical care and medicine is significantly higher compared to charitable hospitals. For example, Renji Hospital only charges 15 copper coins for an outpatient consultation. Inpatient care in a general ward costs only 60 cents a day, including all expenses for food, medical care, and medicine. For major surgeries, a small fee is charged based on the patient's ability to pay, and those who are completely destitute receive free treatment. This truly benefits the common people greatly.

However, the funding for charitable hospitals comes from donations from various sectors of society. Recently, it has been reported that not only is Renji Hospital facing financial difficulties, but other hospitals established by foreigners are also struggling to survive due to dwindling resources. This will have a significant impact on the welfare of the public. The only way to alleviate this situation is to hope that members of society will generously provide financial assistance. This will not only benefit the poor individuals but also benefit society as a whole. The occurrence of disease is a small matter in relation to the pain suffered by individuals but a large matter in relation to public health. For example, Renji Hospital sees as many as 200,000 patients a year. Imagine what would happen if these 200,000 patients were not treated by Renji Hospital and were left to lie down and moan. If some of their illnesses were contagious, the peace and tranquility of society would be unimaginable. This is not only a matter of the health of 200,000 ordinary people. Shanghai philanthropists should pay attention to this and provide practical assistance.

People Living on Garbage Heaps 214

— Shi Xi

Stealthily, stealthily, like a timid rat, I lingered in these corners.

The night was as calm as a pool of stagnant water; it was the late autumn season.

In a window corner reflecting a faint green light, several slender figures were still flickering, and a low song could be heard overhead:

"Tomorrow, you beautiful tomorrow!..."

"Tomorrow"? I murmured softly, "That's still far away!" And then I became angry. The road was bleak, and a faint, indifferent light was blinking like sleepy, bloodshot eyes. I glared at it angrily, shook my fist, and muttered: "Tomorrow? You ghost! Remember, it's tomorrow!..."

I felt so exhausted, and the coldness flowed freely and unrestrainedly in the dark corners. I shivered slightly. "Go to hell!" I muttered angrily to myself, patting myself with my fist in defiance.

Dragging my silent steps, I disappeared again into a dark corner. A strong, pungent odor wafted over, and I frowned and stood still.

"I heard a soft sigh. Yes, a very weak sigh!" I thought to myself, fixed my eyes, and searched in the darkness.

A pile of garbage. "Yes, that's it: overflowing with the stench!" I stared at it blankly for a while before I saw a young man, dressed in rags and emaciated, lying next to it. He was curled up like a worm, clutching a broken tin can with his withered hands. He was mumbling in his sleep, his voice so weak that it made one's heart tremble: "Give me something to eat!..."

"Go to hell! This is also a place to sleep"? I frowned angrily and took a step closer to him.

He was sighing softly, and after a while, he weakly cried out: "Give me something to eat! Just a little bit, enough to fill a crack in my teeth!" As he spoke, he feigned tearless sobs.

Page 20

"Still pretending, damn it!" I thought to myself and couldn't help but sneer. So I tiptoed closer and kicked him lightly on the buttocks, shouting loudly: "Damn it! Go to hell!" His thin body trembled slightly and he woke up.

"Ah!..." he exclaimed in surprise, opening his sleepy eyes, and prepared to jump up suddenly and stride away.

I quickly stopped him and said: "Don't move!" He obediently huddled up and trembled slightly.

"Damn it! What kind of dream were you having"? I cursed him loudly and then laughed coldly.

"Ah! God knows what's going on? Maybe I dreamed again that a wealthy gentleman secretly slipped a silver dollar into my hand. Really, I keep dreaming that someone is giving me a silver dollar... But when I wake up, there's nothing, nothing..." After saying this, he sadly hung his head and secretly stared at me fixedly with his bloodshot eyes. After a while, he turned to the street lamp at the corner, blinked his eyes in anger, yawned resentfully, lay down, and fell asleep again.

I felt a wave of lonely melancholy in my heart, murmured softly: "Go to hell!" and stepped away towards the dim light.

Mr. Du Jiutian's Calligraphy and Painting Two 215

Calligraphy 216

— Meng Hua

Recently, due to some unexpected event, I lost over a hundred books.

Books have always been a luxury for me. For someone who has difficulty even solving their daily living, buying books, especially foreign books, is really an excessive desire. However, when reading is as necessary to me as eating and sleeping in my daily life, and when the books you want to read cannot be found in even the so-called well-equipped libraries, I have no choice but to find ways to exchange the money I saved from eating, clothing, and rent for the books I want to read. In the process, I changed from having meals provided to cooking for myself, from living in an apartment to living in a people’s house, wore my gown until it was tattered, and even tried hard to quit smoking, saving as much money as possible. All of this was for the sole purpose of buying the books I wanted to read. Over the past three years, I have bought over a hundred books and magazines. Although this is pitifully few, I have at least made my best effort.

Because of the difficulty in getting opportunities to buy books, I was very careful when buying them. When I had free time after work, I would take the time to go to the market or the book stalls, trying my best to find the books I wanted to read in the piles of old books. Sometimes I would spend three or four hours without finding a single book worth buying. Even if I found one I liked, I would have to bargain with the clerks. Therefore, obtaining these books not only cost me all the money I had saved, but also took a lot of my energy. Not to mention my detailed notes and annotations.

However, the books that I exchanged for my hard work, now not one is left. Perhaps they have fallen into the hands of old book dealers, or perhaps they have been torn down to wrap peanuts. Maybe they will be placed on the desks of young masters as a not-so-rare decoration, or maybe they have long been buried in the fire. Thinking of these things, I feel unspeakable pain.

I remember once a friend in misfortune wanted me to visit him and asked me to give him something to eat. At that time, I had not a penny in my pocket, so I had to take a copy of "Crime and Punishment" to sell. When the owner of the old bookstore looked at it and offered me a price of forty cents, I felt so angry in my heart. Later, I finally added something else to exchange for a dollar, and bought my friend what he needed. If I had known that these books would have such a day, why didn't I sell them all and let my friend, who was suffering from all kinds of punishments, get more material enjoyment?

Now I have finally moved to this place where I have no relatives. In a corner of a building, surrounded by the noise of the market. In the morning, the sound of the barrows rolling on the stone road wakes me up, and then I begin to wait for dusk. The smell of the tannery next door, where sheepskin is made, blows in with the hot wind and fills my small room, making it unbearable to vomit. In addition, there is only the buzzing of flies and the knocking of the delivery guy. I have nothing to do all day, either immersed in the sea of meditation or greedily reading the old newspapers pasted on the wall. If I had a book or a magazine at this time, wouldn't it be more lovely than a good friend? But I don't have a single book!

In this way, my indignation and hatred grow with the memories of losing my books.

On the Road 217

— Lin Xi

Wen pointed to the square city by the setting sun: "Fangcheng is here." In the dust sinking in the sunset, I saw the old small enemy building, and my heart was naturally happy. I suggested to Wen that we should rest in Fangcheng for a while. My stomach was really hungry. I walked for almost twelve hours, eating only five or six boiled eggs in the middle. I hoped that Fangcheng would arrive early so that I could rest for a while; but the road was always so long, without a head or a tail, high stretching up the hillside, low lying in the ravine, always like this; we doubted whether we had lost our direction, otherwise why hadn't the calculated Fangcheng arrived yet? It was dust, it was wind, it was tiredness, and the whole body was like this, and it was time to wash off the dust and rest.

Looking forward to the early arrival of Fangcheng, I thought of a poem: Drinking horses crossing autumn water, the water is cold and the wind is like a knife, the sun has not set on the flat sand, and the dark Linhuai is seen... I had the mood of a frontier soldier.

On both sides of the road were sorghum fields, and the dense shadows slanted by the setting sun stretched very far, very far. Some of the sorghum had been cut, and the remaining stalks had not been pulled out, which made me think of rows of swords and guns, and we were also somewhat like an expeditionary army. In the distance, someone was driving away the sparrows: Ah! Ah! The sparrows took off, chirping and noisy, turning in a large group on the top of the sorghum, which was also quite beautiful.

Looking at the half-collapsed ancient enemy building of Fangcheng, my heart felt quite kind. When people are too lonely, even a bird or beast feels kind; after hurrying on the empty road for almost twelve hours, all I encountered were dilapidated villages, earthen yellow dilapidated walls, and half-dead willows, how lonely! Although it was just a small city tower, but that heroic posture like an ancient general, rising up in the wilderness as if unwilling to be lonely, gave me a lot of comfort.

At this time, Jiao felt quite excited. I really admired his interest. He looked at the top of the building and hummed Beijing opera: "...First, Ma Di has no courage and little talent, and second, the generals are not harmonious, and then they lost Jieting..." He kept humming until "If you don't come, come, come, please come upstairs and listen to me play the zither" and placed me in another kind of imagination. The vigorous tone disappeared into the twilight, and we entered the city.

It was really tiring, and the blisters on my feet had already broken. When I sat down on the earthen plank outside the small teahouse, my whole body felt sore and lazy, and my thighs were even more painful! Thinking that there was still a long forty miles to go, and looking at the setting sun on the top of the mountain, I really didn't want to go any further; but the toughness of the young people still made us want to go forward. When I pulled up my sore and numb legs, I privately nailed a sentence in my heart: "Swallowing the bitterness in my heart in loneliness, go." So I walked out of Fangcheng with the setting sun on my back.

Looking at the watch, it was half past six, and we had been walking for twelve hours. I thought to myself that it would probably be half an hour before it got dark. Looking back, the setting sun had entered the mountain; "We have to get to Taiping Village before dark." I said, and quickened my pace. The road was extremely bad, the wind scraped the sorghum, rustling, and our footsteps were also rustling, as if someone was following behind. The setting sun had entered the mountain, and there was a sunset glow in the sky; the top of the mountain accepted the sunset glow, reflecting each other differently, which was quite beautiful; but we were not in the mood to appreciate it, and we still had a long way to go.

Passing Taiping Village, it was completely dark. Taiping Village was so peaceful that there was not a single light, and the scattered earth houses looked like piles of earth under the stars. There was no human voice, no barking of dogs. I have experience of passing through villages at night, I have heard the lights shooting out from the bottom of the door, and I have heard the village dogs inquiring about the guests from afar; none of these were in Taiping Village, which was beyond my expectations, and I have never seen such a dead village.

The dead silence made us scared. We were walking while watching the stars. The road was always so long, without a head or a tail. We were waiting for the moon. The date was the eighteenth of the lunar calendar, and the moon should be coming up soon. We sat on the earthen pile by the roadside smoking cigarettes, waiting for the moon to hurry on the road. The wilderness was silent, and the small insects chirped, making it even more lonely. In the distance: the higher black shadows were trees, the lower ones were patches of crops, and even further was a blur. I thought to myself that this was probably the most beautiful time in the poor countryside, all the dead and dilapidated scenery was hidden under the night, and it should be the most beautiful time. If it were daytime, the scorching sun would be burning, and the crops would look like fire from afar, and the dust would be higher than the sky no matter where they were, and the people who managed the vehicles and horses would be covered in dust, struggling in the dust under the scorching sun like earthworms, which was a portrayal of the lives of the residents in this area! These are not visible at night.

The bright moon comes out of Tianshan, and the vast sea of clouds... Seeing the moonlight in the distant mountains, I recalled the ancient poems I learned when I was in elementary school, and treading on the moonlight, I hurried forward again.

Shen Bao Local Supplement - Automobile Weekly

New Trends in Steam Cars and Diesel Cars 226

— Zhenmin

In recent years, various gasoline engines in various countries have developed extremely rapidly. The rate of increase in gasoline consumption has accelerated. It really has a trend beyond everything. According to the results of geological surveys over the years. The world's reserves of kerosene are gradually depleting. This statistic. Of course, it gives a major blow to the future of gasoline cars. Engineers around the world have been working hard in recent years to study new fuel problems for automobiles. Alcohol, charcoal, artificial kerosene, etc. have been successfully tested. But using this fuel to power cars. There are always various difficulties and obstacles. For example, when using charcoal as fuel. It is always difficult to avoid delays in time. Difficulties such as igniting and braking. Such as alcohol. It will also have the same disadvantage of braking difficulties. As for using artificial kerosene. The equipment cost during refining is too high. The economic problems of driving. It is very difficult to solve. In this difficult situation. Engineers have gradually shifted their gaze. Engage in fundamental exploration. And our automobile ancestor, the "steam car." Has once again been noticed by general engineers. Because this type of car has various advantages and conveniences. It is really unmatched by other vehicles. In recent years, there have been extraordinary achievements in the design improvements of this type of vehicle. In addition to this "steam car." There is also the diesel car, which is being enthusiastically researched by general engineers. Now, let's describe their recent progress and trends separately below.

(1) New Trends in Steam Cars The invention of the steam car. As early as 1878 (Western calendar). Earlier than any other car. The initial design was very simple. There was only a boiler and cylinder. And - all the switches. It wasn't until 1895 in the Western calendar. Fangcai had a more thorough plan. But the speed and all the equipment. Still has not been improved. This is really the pioneering period of steam cars. In the past five years, world engineers have made amazing achievements in improving steam cars. The steam engine used. It is a kind of most ingenious and latest type. The size of this engine is 4" × 5". It can be directly connected to the rear axle. Without using gears, etc. for transmission. Because there is a constant steam supply. Therefore, at any vehicle speed. Can have the highest capacity. There has also been very precise progress in the structure of the engine's valves. Steam input. Can be adjusted very finely. Boilers are all fire-tube type. Can have a pressure of more than 500 pounds. In the past. European and American - ordinary "gentlemen". I thought this mobile boiler. Are very dangerous. And opposed. In fact, this concept is a huge mistake. Because on 20th century boilers. Equipped with many safety designs. Even more on this boiler used in cars. Absolutely no danger will occur. The biggest advantage of steam cars. It is simple in construction and very convenient to brake. And when driving. There is absolutely no noise. The supply of fuel does not depend on kerosene. Only coal and water are sufficient. In terms of economy. Of course, it is much cheaper. At the same time, because of the simple mechanical structure. The manufacturing cost is very low. This all - all. Is something that gasoline cars cannot match. In recent years, there has been a rapid trend in the improvement of various components on the car. For example, the excellent use of electrical systems. The ingenious combustion furnace. High efficiency of the vacuum brake, etc. The extreme streamlining of the car body is no longer a problem. According to statistical results. Of the cars registered in the United States in 1933. 3.5% are steam cars. In 1934 it was 15%. This year to date. Steam cars account for 21.8%. This rapid rate of increase. It's really amazing. It is expected that future achievements. There is even more fierce progress.

(2) New Trends in Diesel Cars Because of the high price of gasoline. Diesel cars have gradually replaced gasoline cars in recent years. If the same car uses diesel as fuel. The cost per mile of driving can be reduced by 56%. So the development of diesel cars in recent years. Unusually rapid. The increase in engine compression. Make the efficiency particularly outstanding. Although the fuel for diesel cars comes from kerosene. But because it does not require refining. Once kerosene runs out. Can be extracted from coal. This is more convenient and economical than refining gasoline. In the American car races in the past two years. Diesel cars have made significant progress in increasing speed. The strong engine structure. Makes the compression particularly increased. And because of the ingenious fuel injector and braking mechanism. Makes braking unexpectedly convenient. The streamlining of the car body. Makes the car shape more aesthetically pleasing and reduces air pressure. According to statistical results. The life of a diesel engine. More durable than a gasoline engine. This is due to design and factual needs. In the current situation. The price of diesel engines. A little more expensive. But the average driving cost. But it is much cheaper. In the 1934 American cars. 30% are diesel engines. Germany already has more than 40%. The future trend. Perhaps all gasoline cars. Will be replaced by this diesel car.

This Year's Millionth Commemorative Car from Two Major Companies 228

— Yu

General Motors' Chevrolet General Motors recently completed its millionth car of 1935. The completion period. It was 64 days earlier than last year's completion period. However, according to GM Vice President Knudson. The working procedures for 1936. It will be larger and faster than this year. Regarding sales. According to Sales Director Vice President Grande. The sales volume next year will also increase compared to this year. In short, the prospects for both production sides. They are all optimistic and upward. One year is better than one year. This year's millionth General Motors car. It is a Chevrolet's luxurious city sedan. At the beginning of August. It was completed and left the factory. Last year's millionth General Motors car. It was not released until October 10th. So this year's millionth completion period. It is more than two months faster than last year. This year's millionth car. Its number is among the Chevrolet cars that produce 5,600 vehicles per day. It ranks number 1,384. The engine number is 5, 4 Tai 2, 112. However, the production number. Does not include Obordon. The Bili Zhi freight cars manufactured in Germany. And the Bedford freight cars in the UK are included. Speaking of the market development in 1936. Knudson and Grande have the same opinion. That is, the current average selling price. It will still maintain the status quo next year. Reducing prices is unlikely to become a reality. Increasing the selling price is even more impossible. The reason for this is that the cost of labor and raw materials. Can maintain stability. And the decline in raw materials. Will not become possible. According to Knudson. Ford's V8 The 2 millionth V8 Ford – the millionth Ford completed in less than twelve months, and approximately the 23,000,000th Ford – was completed on July 13th of this year at the Ford Motor Company's Rouge plant. Ford's founder, Henry Ford, and Ford Motor Company President Edsel Ford, both witnessed the final assembly of this historically valuable Ford. Once this two-millionth Ford left the factory. It began its 2,700-mile long journey. Straight to San Diego, California. There, this car. It will be displayed in the Ford display at the California Pacific International Exposition. Since June 19, 1934. Since the Ford factory completed the millionth Ford. Another million vehicles were completed in less than a year. This confirms what Ford said at the end of last year. That is, Ford Motor Company "will exceed one million units in 1935." This 2,000,000th V8 Ford. It is the fourth historically significant Ford to cross the continent. These four cars. Between the Atlantic and Pacific coasts. Have all worked on one of the four major highways to promote it. The earliest can be traced back to 1909. A T-style Ford. At that time, it was a newcomer in the automotive industry. And it was soon destined to become the most famous car. It marched from New York to Seattle. At the cross-continental car race that ended at the Alaska Yukon Pacific Exposition. Won the Guggenheim Medal. Ford personally congratulated the car that won the paddle at the finish line. The second historically significant Ford. Belongs to No. 10,000,000, also a T-type. Completed in 1924 after leaving the Highland Park factory. Then from New York, it went straight to San Francisco via the Lincoln Highway. The third historically valuable one. It is an A-type car. Belongs to No. 20,000,000. Completed in 1931 at the Rouge plant. After arriving in New York. Then from there to Los Angeles and San Francisco. The fourth historical record Ford. It is the 1,000,000th V8 Ford. Completed on June 19 last year at the Rouge plant, it was driven to Chicago and then displayed in the Ford display at the Century of Progress Exposition.

Overview of the Guangxi Provincial Highway 229

— Yong

Guangxi's highways began in the 7th year of the Republic of China. At that time, the Yongwu Road, which was 120 li long. First start construction. The Longnan Road, which is 90 li long, followed. After the 10th year of the Republic of China. Yongbin and Wubo roads both identified sorting out traffic as the basis for improving all government affairs. Therefore, highways in Yongliu, Guiwu, Zhentian and other regions were built one after another. After several years of generous management. Thousands of miles of highways were built in the overlapping mountains. In the past, the rugged and obstructed. To this end, the main roads in various districts have been opened one after another. Not only have culture and economy developed considerably. The implementation of politics. The progress of military affairs. Also receive good results. However, land transportation. Railways must be the main trunk. Connected with provincial, county and township roads. Make the veins communicate. And the effect is grand. In the past, due to time and economic relations. Railways have not yet started construction. County and township roads. Also failed to be held at the same time. In the 18th and 19th years of the Republic of China. Also because of social unrest. Everything came to a standstill. After the 20th year of the Republic of China, the provincial government reported stability again. The government is working hard to govern. Everything construction. Nothing is extremely sharp. In terms of road administration. The provincial roads that need to be urgently added, such as Baiping. Danchi. Yongqin. Cheda. Wuben. Each line. It has now been completed one after another. Mianliu Yong. Baidu. Limeng. Various lines. Are also being planned for construction. The rest of the county and township roads have also been revised and planned. Now either it has been completed. Or actively carry out. As for the railway. Line survey work has also been carried out. And plan construction. This is roughly the past and present situation of Guangxi's road administration. Now I will describe the general outline of the completed highways in this province. And future construction plans. In order,

(1) Guangxi Highway that has been completed Prior to the 20th year of the Republic of China, the districts of Nanning, Zhennan, Liujiang, Guilin, Cangwu, and Tiannan were established and managed separately. Since the unification of road administration a year ago, in addition to the road affairs of Yongzhen District being directly handled by the Highway Administration, each of the other districts of Gui, Liu, Wu, and Tian has an office. Everything is buried nearby. Now the province's highways have been completed. Nanning District 3,338 li. Zhennan District 1,537 li. Liujiang District 2,720 li. Guilin District 2,294 li. Cangwu District 1,755 li. Tiannan District 691 li. The total number of highways completed in the province is 12,341 li. Among them, provincial roads are 6,443 li. County roads are 5,898 li. If you enter Guangxi from Hong Kong and Guangdong and transfer to Annam. You can take a car from Rongxu to Longzhou in two days. You can enter Vietnam in three days. If you transfer to Guizhou, you can reach Qingyuan or Hechi in two days. You can enter Qian in three days. If you transfer to Hunan. You can reach Liuzhou or Lipu in two days. You can reach Guilin or Quanzhou in three days. You can enter Xiang in four days. For example, Annam enters Guangxi. Pass through Nanning and transfer to Xiangqian. You can take a car from Longzhou. Reach Liuzhou or Qingyuan in two days. Reach Guilin or Qianbian in three days. In the past four days. There is really a world of difference.
